Watumiaji wa mtandao wa intaneti wa nchini Iran wameanzisha vurugu kubwa mtandaoni baada ya kupata habari ya kusikitisha ya kifo cha mwanablogu aliyefia gerezani iliyowekwa kwa mara ya kwanza mtandaoni na tovuti za upinzani. ||| Iranian netizens have launched a major online storm after the shocking news of a blogger's death in custody was first posted by opposition websites.
Kwa mujibu wa mahojiano na watu wa wafimilia ya Sattar Beheshti na pia taarifa kutoka katika tovuti za haki za binadamu, mwanablogu huyu alikamatwa mnamo tarehe 28 Oktoba, 2012 na takribani siku kumi baadae, alitangazwa kuwa amefariki. ||| According to interviews with Sattar Beheshti's family members as well as reports on human rights websites, he was arrested on October 28, 2012 and announced dead some ten days after his arrest.
Wafungwa 41 wa kisiasa bravely walichapisha kwa weledi mkubwa taarifa iliyokuwa inasema walishuhudia dalili za kuteswa katika mwili wa Sattar. ||| 41 political prisoners bravely published a statement saying they witnessed signs of torture on Sattar's body.
Mashirika mbalimbali ya kimataifa ikiwa ni pamoja na waandishi wa habari wasio na mipaka maalum wameishinikiza mamlaka ya Iran kutoa ufafanuzi wa kina wa mzingira ya kifo cha mwanablogu huyu na kuzitaka jamii za kimataifa kutokukubali kosa hili kumalizwa bila ya wahusika kuadhibiwa. ||| Several international organizations including Reporters Without Borders urged the Iranian authorities to clarify the exact circumstances of the blogger's death and called on the international community not to allow the crime to go unpunished.
Uanaharakati wa mawsiliano wa Beheshti, ikiwa ni pamoja na blogu yake mwenyewe umeonekana dhahiri kuwa ndio uliompelekea kuwekwa kukamatwa kikatili, kuteswa na hatimaye kuuawa akiwa na umri wa miaka 35. ||| Beheshti's cyber-activism, including his personal blog apparently led to his brutal arrest, torture and eventual death at the age of 35.

Ifuatayo ni ya kwanza katika mlolongo wa makala zinazounga mkono kampeni ya kuchangisha fedha kwenye mtandao ili kutunishamfuko wa Global Voices mwaka 2009-10. ||| The following is a first in a series of posts in support of Global Voices' 2009-10 online fundraising campaign.

Mkurugenzi wa Sauti Zinazokua, David Sasaki ameandika kumbukumbu ya kuvutia kwa ajili ya siku ya kuadhimisha miaka mitano ya Global Voices. ||| Rising Voices Director David Sasaki has written a lovely retrospective for Global Voices' fifth birthday.
Miaka mitano iliyopita mwezi huu, David alisafiri katika Marekani kuanzia California mpaka Havard kwa ajili ya warsha ya siku nzima kuhusu kublogu ulimwenguni. ||| Five years ago this month, David traveled across the United States from California to Harvard for a day-long workshop on global blogging.
Tovuti unayoisoma leo ilianza kama blogu ambayo Ethan Zuckerman na mimi tuliitengeneza ili kuandaa warsha hiyo. ||| The website you are reading today started out as a blog that Ethan Zuckerman and I set up to organize that workshop.
Lengo letu, tukiliweka kirahisi, lilikuwa kujadili jinsi ya kutumia kublogu na zana za kublogu ili kuwasaidia watu katika nchi tofauti kufanya mazungumzo yenye maana na ya moja kwa moja baina yao.ù ||| Our aim, put very simply, was to discuss how to use blogging and blog tools to help people in different countries hold more meaningful and direct conversations with each other.ù 
Majadiliano ya siku hiyo yalikuwa ni sehemu ya kongamano kubwa la Wavuti na Jamii lililoandaliwa na Kituo cha Berkman cha Wavuti na Jamii chuoni Harvard. ||| The day's discussion was part of a larger Internet and Society conference put on by Harvard's Berkman Center for Internet and Society.
Taasisi ya Jamii Wazi kwa ukarimu ilitufadhili fedha kiasi ili kuwasafirisha wanablogu kutoka sehemu mbalimbali duniani. ||| The Open Society Institute generously granted us some funds to fly in bloggers from various parts of the world.
Tulilitangaza tukio hilo kwenye wavuti, na wengine wengi, kama David, walijitokeza. ||| We publicized the event on the web, and many others, like David, just showed up.
Tunashukuru. ||| Thank goodness.
Hii ni makala niliyoiandika mara baada ya mkutano. ||| Here is an article I wrote soon after the meeting.
Hii ni posti ya blogu ya Ethan siku iliyofuata.ù Hatukutoka na mpango mahsusi wa kuitawala dunia, au hata mradi thabiti. ||| Here is Ethan's day afterù blog post. We did not emerge with a concrete plan for world domination, or even for a coherent project.
Washiriki walikubaliana kuanzisha ukurasa wa ushirika katika wavuti ili kushirikiana habari, pamoja na Mazungumzo ya Maandishi Kwenye Wavuti (IRC) kwa ajili ya mikutano mingine kwenye wavuti, pamoja na kikusanya blogu kitakachoendeshwa na washiriki wa kongamano pamoja na wengine kama wao ambao tulianza kuwaita wanablogu kiungo.ù Hatukuwa na hakika tungeelekea wapi baada ya pale. ||| Participants agreed to set up a wiki to share information, an Internet Relay Chat (IRC) for further on-line meetings, and an aggregator of blogs by conference participants and others like them who we began to call bridge bloggers.ù We weren't sure where we would go from there.
Jambo moja, hata hivyo, lilikuwa wazi: umma amuzi wa wanablogu wenye maadili yanayofanana na yetu ulikuwa unaanza kujitokeza duniani kote. ||| One thing, however, was clear: a critical mass of bloggers with similar values was emerging around the globe.
Ilionekana kama ni wazo zuri kuunganisha nukta zoteù (kama Jeff Ooi anavyosema) baina ya watu hawa na kuunda jukwaa linalotokana na jamii hii inayokua. ||| It seemed like a good idea to connect the dotsù (as Jeff Ooi put it) amongst these people and create a platform for this emergent community.
Katika majuma yaliyofuata baada ya kongamano, baadhi ya washiriki walitumia ukurasa wa ushirika kwenye wavuti ili kuyaweka maadili ya jamii hii. ||| In the weeks following the conference, a number of participants used a wiki to articulate this community's shared values.
Matokeo yake yalikuwa ni Ilani ya Global Voices. ||| The Global Voices Manifesto was the result.
Ni muhimu kuiweka tena hapa katika ujumla wake kwani kila kitu ambacho Global Voices inakifanya leo hii kinaendelea kuendeshwa na maadili hayo ya msingi: ||| It's worth reproducing in full here because everything Global Voices does today continues to be driven by these fundamental values:
Tunaamini katika uhuru wa kujieleza, katika kulinda haki ya kutoa kauli, na haki ya kusikiliza. ||| We believe in free speech, in protecting the right to speak, and the right to listen.
Tunaamini katika upati huru wa nyenzo za kujieleza. ||| We believe in universal access to the tools of speech.
Ili kufanikisha hilo, tanataka kumwezesha kila mmoja ambaye anataka kujieleza kuwa na njia za kujieleza, na kila mmoja anayetaka kusikiliza, awe na njia za kusikiliza. ||| To that end, we seek to enable everyone who wants to speak to have the means to speak, and everyone who wants to hear that speech, the means to listen to it.
Shukrani kwa nyezo mpya, kauli hazihitaji kudhibitiwa na wale wanaomiliki njia za uchapishaji na usambazaji, au na serikali ambazo zinaweza kudhibiti fikra na mawasiliano. ||| Thanks to new tools, speech need no longer be controlled by those who own the means of publishing and distribution, or by governments that would restrict thought and communication.
Hivi sasa, mtu yeyote anaweza kuwa na nguvu za vyombo vya habari. ||| Now, anyone can wield the power of the press.
Kila mtu anaweza kusimulia simulizi yake kwa dunia. ||| Everyone can tell their stories to the world.
Tunataka kujenga madaraja katika mabonde yanayotenganisha watu, ili kwamba tuweze kuelewana zaidi. ||| We seek to build bridges across the gulfs that divide people, so as to understand each other more fully.
Tanataka kufanya kazi kwa ufanisi zaidi, na kutenda kwa nguvu zaidi. ||| We seek to work together more effectively, and act more powerfully.
Tunaamini katika nguvu ya kukutana moja kwa moja. ||| We believe in the power of direct connection.
Mshikamano kati ya watu kutoka dunia tofauti niwa kibinafsi, kisiasa na wenye nguvu. ||| The bond between individuals from different worlds is personal, political and powerful.
Tunaamini kuwa maongezi yanashinda mipaka ni muhimu kwa mustakabali ambo ni huru, wa haki, wenye kuneemesha na endelevu kwa raia wote wa dunia hii. ||| We believe conversation across boundaries is essential to a future that is free, fair, prosperous and sustainable for all citizens of this planet.
Huku tukiendelea kufanya kazi na kuongea kama watu binafsi, pia tunataka kutambua na kukuza malengo na maslahi tunayoshirikiana pamoja. ||| While we continue to work and speak as individuals, we also seek to identify and promote our shared interests and goals.
Tunaahidi kuheshimu, kusaidia, kufundisha, kujifunza na kusikiliza kutoka kwa kila mmoja wetu. ||| We pledge to respect, assist, teach, learn from, and listen to one other.
Sisi ni Sauti za Dunia. ||| We are Global Voices.
Hivi sasa tuna timu ya watu wa mataifa mbalimbali ambao wanashika nafasi kama wasimamizi wa sehemu mbalimbali za Global Voices. ||| We now have an amazing multinational team who act as stewards for various parts of Global Voices.
Lakini roho ya ya GV ni mamia ya watu wanaojitolea ambao wanatenga muda kutoka kwenye kazi zao, masomo, na majukumu ya kifamilia ili kusaidia kujenga majadiliano ya umma wa dunia yaliyo huru zaidi na shirikishi. ||| But the soul of GV are the hundreds of volunteers who take time out from their jobs, studies, and and family obligations to help build a more open and participatory global public discourse.
Wanachama wa jamii ya Global Voices katika Mkutano wa Delhi India, mwaka 2006. ||| Members of the Global Voices community at the 2006 Summit in Delhi, India.
Habari kuhusu mradi huu zipo hapa. ||| News stories about the project are here.
Tunatazamia kuwa na mkutano mwingine mwaka 2010 (mahali na tarehe vitatangazwa hivi karibuni). ||| We are looking forward to another gathering in 2010 (location and date to be announced soon).
Mwaka 2006 mimi na Ethan tuliandika makala kwa ajili ya jarida la Nieman Reports ambamo tulitaka kuelezea uhusiano kati ya Global Voices na uanahabari. ||| In 2006 Ethan and I wrote an article for the Nieman Reports magazine in which we sought to explain the relationship between Global Voices and journalism.
David anayo makala nyingine nzuri sana inayohusu kwa nini shughuli za kivuko, utetezi na ufasiri ni muhimukatika kuwasaidia watu kuvishinda vikwazo vya kuongea, kisikilizwa, na kuwasikiliza wengine. ||| David has another excellent post about why outreach, advocacy and translation are necessary to help people overcome the obstacles to speaking, being heard, and listening to others.
Watu wengi duniani wanakerwa kwa kuwa vyombo vya habari vikuu vya kiingereza duniani havitilii maanani nchi zao kwa muda mrefu, na kuandika tu habari mbaya kuhusu nchi zao, au vyombo hivyo huendeleza tu imani potofu kuwahusu. ||| Many people around the world are frustrated that the global English-language mainstream media ignores their country much of the time, or only covers the bad things about their country, or tends to stereotype them.
Wanaiona GV kama jukwaa la thamani ambalo wanaweza kukuza simulizi na mitazamo yao kwa hadhira pana zaidi duniani. ||| They see GV as a valuable platform through which to get their stories and viewpoints amplified to a broader global audience.
Wengine wanakereka na kwamba vyombo vya habari vya ndani ya nchi zao vinashindwa kuripoti juu ya sehemu nyingi za dunia, wanafanya vibaya, au wanaripoti katika namna iliyopinda ambayo inaunga mkono mtazamo wa dunia wa serikali zao, na hivyo wanaamini kuwa kwa kutafsiri maudhui ya GV katika lugha zao za nyumbani wanaweza kuboresha ufahamu wa dunia wa jamii zao. ||| Others are frustrated that their own domestic news media fail to report on much of the world, do it badly, or do it in a slanted manner that supports their government's worldview, and thus believe that by translating GV content into their local language they can improve their community's understanding of the world.
Wengine wanatilia makini kuzisaidia jamii ambazo hazijachukua hatua za kunufaika na teknolojia mpya ili kuzitoa simulizi zao nje. ||| Others focus on helping communities who are not yet taking advantage of new technologies to get their story out.
Wengine wamejiunga kwa dhumuni la pamoja dhidi ya kuchuja habari na ukandamizwaji wa wale ambao wanatumia haki yao ya kujieleza kwa uhuru kwa mujibu wa kipengele cha 19 cha Azimio la Umoja wa Mataifa la Haki za Binadamu. ||| Others have joined in common cause against censorship and repression of those who are merely exercising their universal right to free expression according to Article 19 of the United Nations Universal Declaration of Human Rights.
Jamii ya GV haijaruhusu kujikwamisha katika mijadala isiyoisha kama wanablogu ni wanahabari au la, au wavuti unamaanisha nini katika biashara ya habari. ||| The GV community has not let itself get bogged down in endless debates about whether bloggers are or aren't journalists, or what the Internet means for the news business.
Kadhalika GV haijifungi katika mizozo kuhusu je Wavuti utakuwa ni nguvu ya demokrasi duniani au la. ||| Nor does GV get tangled up in arguments about whether the Internet is or is not going to be a force for global democratization.
Kama jamii tunatilia mkazo kukunja mikono ya mashati yet una kuingia kazini ili kukabiliana na tatizo hai zaidi: kuziba mapengo yaliyo kwenye mjadala wa umma duniani, na kufanya tunaloweza kuhusu mizani isiyo sawa, uonevu na ukiukwaji wa haki katika vyombo vya habari duniani. ||| As a community we're more interested in rolling up our sleeves and getting to work addressing a more tangible problem: filling a few of the gaping holes in the global public discourse, and doing what we can about the huge imbalances, inequities, and injustices in global media.
Haijalishi namna utakavyobainisha kazi hii, tunaamini kuwa kile tunachokifanya kina thamani na kinabadilisha mambo. ||| However you define this work, we believe that what we're doing has value and makes a difference.
Tunashukuru kwamba mashirika kadhaa yameiona kazi yetu kuwa ina thamani kwa ufadhili wao kifedha. ||| We are grateful that a range of organizations have deemed our work to be worthy of their financial support.
Tumeendeleza uhusiano na vyombo vya habari ambavyo vinafuatilia kazi zetu na kututaka kwa sababu kwa namna yoyote utakavyoeleza tunachofanya jamii yet uni chanzo chenye thamani cha habari za dunia na mitazamo mipya. ||| We have developed relationships with news organizations who follow our work and seek us out because however you define what we do our community is a valuable source of global information and fresh perspectives.
Hii ni sababu ambayo Reuters ilitoa usaidizi wa kiini katika miaka yetu mitatu ya kwanza, na sababu ambayo mashirika mengi ya habari yanaendelea kufanya kazi na wahariri wet una kuwasiliana na watu wanaojitolea kwa ajili ya mahojiano. ||| This is why Reuters provided critical core support in our first three years, and why a many news organizations continue to work with our editors and to contact our volunteers for interviews.
Wakati hatuwezi kusema kuwa tumebadilisha kabisa uanahabari wa ulimwengu, tunaamini kuwa tumeweza kuyaelekeza macho ya vyombo vya habari kwenye habari nyingi ambazo vinginevyo zisingeweza kuripotiwa, na kutoa mitazamo mipya juu ya hamari nyingi za kimataifa. ||| While we can't say we've completely transformed global media, we do believe that we've brought global media attention to a range of stories that might otherwise not have been reported, and provided fresh perspectives on numerous other major international news stories.
Jambo hilo pekee limeifanya jitihada hii kuwa ya thamani. ||| That in itself has made the entire enterprise worthwhile.
Jambo la kusisimua zaidi ni jinsi Global voices ilivyobadilisha maisha ya wahariri wetu, watu wanaojitolea na jamii pana ya wanachama. ||| What's even more exciting is the way in which Global Voices has impacted the lives of our editors, volunteers, and broader community members.
Tumekuwa kituo ambacho kundi la kuvutia la watu wenye vipaji, werevu na wanaojali wengine hupata kuridhika, kutambuliwa duniani, na usaidizi wa kijamii. ||| We have become a hub through which an amazing group of talented, articulate, and caring people can find fulfillment, global recognition, and community support.
Bonyeza hapa ili kusoma juu ya jinsi ambavyo Sauti Zinazokua ilivyozileta sauti zenye utofauti katika mazungumzo ya kitaifa na ya kidunia, na maana ya jambo hilo kwa watu binafsi na kwa jamii husika. ||| Click here to read about how Rising Voices has brought more diverse voices into national and global conversations, and what that has meant for the individuals and communities involved.
Ili kuapata kionjo cha namna ambavyo waandishi wetu wa kujitolea walivyo, soma na kusikiliza baadhi ya wasifu wa wanablogu hao hapa. ||| To get a sense of how amazing our volunteers are, read and listen to some of the blogger profiles posted here.
GV pia imekuwa na msukumo kwa jamii mbalimbali za wanablogu duniani ambazo tuna uhusiano rasmi nazo zaidi ya kuweka viunganishi na kutafsiri baadhi ya makala zao za kwenye blogu katika wakati tofauti tofauti. ||| GV has also had an impact on various blogging communities around the world with whom we have no formal relationship other than linking to and translating some of their blog posts from time to time.
Mfano mmoja tu: Ethan hivi karibuni alielezea mazungumzo yanayofungua macho na mwanablogu kijana wa jamii ya Kyrgiz, Bektour Iskander kuhusu athari za baadhi ya kazi zetu huko Asia ya Kati. ||| Just one example: Ethan recently described an eye-opening conversation with a young Kyrgyz blogger, Bektour Iskender about the impact some of our work has had in Central Asia.
Kile kitakachotokea kutoka katika mazingira ya uanahabari duniani yaliyo na demokrasia zaidi kidogo, yaliyo wazi na shirikishi bado hakijajulikana wazi. ||| What might result from a slightly more democratic, open, and participatory global media environment is not clear.
Katika mkutano wa 2004, mwanablogu wa Kiirani Hossein Derakhshan alielezea matumaini kwamba kuenea kwa uanahabari wa kiraia kwenye wavuti kutazifanya jamii kuwa za kidemokrasi zaidi na kwa serikali kuapta ugumu zaidi katika kuhalalisha vita. ||| At the 2004 meeting, Iranian blogger Hossein Derakhshan expressed the hope that the spread of online citizen media would make societies more democratic and war more difficult for governments to justify.
Hoderù kama anavyojulikana kwenye wavuti, amefungwa na utawala wa Amhedinejad kwa zaidi ya mwaka mmoja sasa, haieleweki kama uhusiano mpana kati ya Wairani na Wamagharibi utakuwa ndiyo sababu kuu katika uamuzi wa Marekani wa ama kuivamia au kutoivamia Irani. ||| Hoder,ù as he's known on the Internet, has been imprisoned by Ahmedinejad's regime for over a year now, and it's not clear whether expanded contacts between Iranians and Westerners would be a deciding factor in a U.S. decision about whether or not to attack Iran.
Waandishi kama Evgeny Morozov wanadai kuwa kinyume na matumaini ya awali kuhusu wavuti kuwa nguvu ya demokrasi, tawala za kiimla zinang'amua jinsi ya kutumia wavuti ili kuimarisha nguvu zao na kukandamiza upinzani na kwamba wavuti katika nchi nyingi inatawaliwa na upindishaji wa habari, utoaji wa habari potofu na chuki. ||| Writers like Evgeny Morozov argue that contrary to early optimism about the Internet as a democratizing force, dictatorships are figuring out how to use the Internet to solidify their power and suppress dissent and that the Internet in many countries is dominated by manipulated spin, disinformation and hate.
Wengine kama Clay Shirky na Patrick Meier wanadai kwamba bado kuna sababu ya kutumaini. ||| Others like Clay Shirky and Patrick Meier argue that there is still reason for optimism.
Na bado wengine wanaonyesha kuwa wengi wa watu duniani wana matatizo makubwa zaidi kama vile kuishi tu na yote hapo juu pamoja na kazi za Global Voices hazina maana kwao. ||| Still others point out that most of the world's people have more pressing problems like physical survival and all of the above including Global Voices' work is irrelevant to them anyway.
Miaka mitano iliyopita Ory Okolloh ambaye aliendelea na kuanzisha jukwaa lililofanikiwa sana la kuripoti la jamii Ushahidi alitoa maoni fulani yanayopaswa kurejewa katika muktadha wa midahalo hii. ||| Five years ago Ory Okolloh who went on to found the wildly successful citizen reporting platform Ushahidi made some comments that are worth revisiting in the context of those debates.
Hivi ndivyo nilivyoripoti maneno yake wakati huo: ||| Here's how I reported her words at the time:
Mwanablogu wa Kenya Ory Okolloh hategemei kuwa Afrika itabadilishwa na kublogu katika wakati wowote hivi karibuni. ||| Kenyan blogger Ory Okolloh doesn't expect Africa to be transformed by blogging any time soon.
Kuunganisha utengano wa kidijitali pengine ni jambo la chini sana katika matatizo mengi ya Afrika. ||| Bridging the digital divide is perhaps the least of Africa's many problems.
Haidhuru, ory anafikiri kuwa kublogu ni jambo muhimu kama si jambi linalobadilisha kwa idadi ndiogo ya Waafrika wanaoblogu. ||| Nonetheless, she thinks blogging is important if not transformative for the small number of Africans who do blog.
Kwa vijana, hatujasikilizwa, hatuna sehemu katika Afrika ndani ya siasa au katika majukwaa mengine kuweza kujieleza,ù anasema Okolloh. ||| For young people, we have not been heard, we don't have a space in Africa within politics or in other arenas to express ourselves,ù Okolloh says.
Nafikiriinaweza kutoa jukwaa kwa vijana kuunda sehemu yao wenyewe. ||| I think it could provide a forum for young people to create their own space.
Sidhani kama itabadilisha siasa kabisa au itaelekeza uchaguzi bali ninafikiri itaweza kuzaa jamii katika nia ambazo hazijawahi kuweza kutokea kabla.ù ||| I don't think it will change politics per se or determine an election but I think it can breed community in ways that have not been able to take place before.ù
Uanahabari wa kijamii kwenye wavuti unazaa namna mpya za jamii katika ngazi za sehemu husika, kitaifa na kidunia. ||| Online citizen media is breeding new forms of community at the local, national, and global level.
GV imekuwa chembe hai tepe inayonganisha jamii ya wanablogu wa Kikenya ya Ory na wanablogu wengine duniani ambao wanashiriki maadili yanayofanana. ||| GV has become a loose connective tissue between Ory's Kenyan blogging community and other bloggers around the world who share similar values.
Wakati Global Voices ina nia ya kuelekeza habari zinazoripotiwa na vyombo vya habari vya kitamaduni ambavyo vingi vyake vinahudumia mataifa au maeneo malum kadhalika tunajenga jukwaa kwa ajili ya mazungumzo ya kidunia, na jamii ya raia wa dunia katika mazungumzo hayo. ||| While Global Voices seeks to influence the stories reported by traditional news media most of which serve specific nations or regions we are also building a platform for global discourse, and a community of global citizens around that discourse.
Tunatumia wavuti si kwa ajili ya kutoroka kutoka katika ubinadamu wetu, bali kwa ajili ya kuusisitiza. ||| We use the Internet not to escape from our humanity, but to assert it.
Tunaamini kuwa maamuzi binafsi na vitendo vianasababisha mabadiliko. ||| We believe individual choices and actions make a difference.
Ikiwa wavuti hatimaye utawezesha zaidi kuliko unavyotia watu utumwani kutategemea kama tutachukua wajibu kwa ajili ya mustakabali wetu na kutenda. ||| Whether the Internet will ultimately empower more than it enslaves depends on whether we take responsibility for our future and act.
Kujenga jamii ya tamaduni mbalimbali na lugha mbalimbali inayomakinikia miradi mahsusi inayounganishwa na seti ya maadili ya kiutu ni jitihada ndogo katika mwelekeo huo. ||| Building a multi-cultural, multi-lingual community focused on specific projects underpinned by a core set of humanistic values is just one small effort in that direction.
Urusi: Jinsi Abiria wa Nevsky Expressù Walivyoeleza Habari Kupitia Vyombo Vya Habari Vya Kijamii ||| Russia: How Passengers of Nevsky Expressù Tell Their Stories Through Social Media

Na ndipo picha za kwanza na video zilipoanza kuonekana kila mahali. ||| Only then the first photographs and videos started to appear everywhere.

Abira pekee ambaye alitoa taarifa mara moja kuhusu ajali ya Nevsky Expressù alikuwa mtumiaji wa Twita. ||| The only passenger who immediately reported about the crash of Nevsky Expressù was a Twitter user.
Haya ndio aliyoandika: ||| Here is what she wrote:
Nipo hai. ||| I am alive.
Lakini nitaeleza kuhusu (ajali) baadaye. ||| But I should tell about it later.
Kama mtu ataeleza chochote kwenye habari, tafadhali niandikie. ||| If someone tells anything in news, please write me.
Hawatuambii kila kitu hapa. ||| They don't tell us anything here.
Baadaye, abiria wengi kutoka mabehewa ya kwanza ni mabehewa ya mwisho ambayo yaliteguliwa kutoka kwenye reli ìwalisema kuwa kwa saa zima baada ya ajali hawakufahamu chochote. ||| Later, many passengers from first cars only last cars were derailed said they were clueless for the whole hour after the crash.
Tumepanda treni jingine. ||| We boarded another train.
Nilifanya kila nilichoweza. ||| I did whatever I could to help.
Natamani ingekuwa inakwenda polepole. ||| I wish it would go slower.
Wametangaza sasa hivi kuwa watu walitayarishwa rasmi wangetulaki kwenye kituo cha treni. ||| They announced now that specially trained people would meet us at the train station.
Siku iliyofuata baada ya dhahama ||| The day after the tragedy

ambaye alikuwemo ndani ya mabehewa ya mwisho yaliharibiwa vibaya na mlipuko. ||| who was in one of the last cars heavily damaged by an explosion.

Nilikuwa na muda wa kutosha kuutayarisha mwili wangu. ||| I had enough time to prepare my body.
Lakini hakuna linaloweza kusaidia dhidi ya kanuni za Newton wakati dazeni za tani za vyuma zinaposimama mara moja wakati zikiwa katika mwendo wa kasi ni bahati tu kwa hiyo nilikuwa na bahati tu. ||| But nothing can help against the Newton's laws when dozens of tons of metal suddenly stop at high speed just luck  therefore I was just lucky.
Kaka yangu alikuwa na bahati, pia, ukiachilia mbali ukweli kuwa majeraha yake yalikuwa yanatisha kuliko yangu. ||| My brother was lucky, too, despite the fact that his wounds were more serious than mine.
Kila kitu ambacho kilikwenda mrama hadi kusimama kabisa kulichukua kama sekunde 30 hivi. ||| Everything from something that went wrong till the full stop took about 30 seconds.
Ilikuwa giza na kimya. ||| It was dark and silent.
Watu walioumia walianza kulia. ||| Then wounded people started to cry.
Nilikuwa sakafuni, nimekandamizwa na miili mingine. ||| I was on the floor, smashed by other bodies.
Niliisogeza ile miili. ||| I moved the bodies.
Niliona kuwa nimelowana na damu lakini damu ile haikuwa yangu. ||| I saw that I was covered with blood but it wasn't mine.
Kichwani nilikuwa na jeraha linalovuja damu. ||| I had a bleeding wound in my head.

Tulikuwa tumeketi mwishoni mwa behewa na mikoba yote ilipaa ikituelekea. ||| We were sitting at the end of the train car and all the bags flied toward us.
Watu wengi waliojeruhiwa. ||| A lot of wounded people around.
Katika dakika chahce baada ya ajali, behewa lilikuwa ni kama fungu la miili, viti na sehemu za treni ambazo zilikuwa zimesambaa sawia kila mahali. ||| During the first minutes after the crash, the car was just a buch of bodies, chairs and parts of the train that were equally distributed around.

behewa lake halikuharibiwa na mlipuko. ||| Her train car was not damaged by the explosion.

Jumamosi, alichapisha habari nzima kuhusu ajali kama alivyoshudia mwenyewe: ||| On Saturday, published the whole story of the crash as she witnessed it:
Tulihisi mitetemo michache ambayo ilikuwa ikiongezeka nguvu. ||| We felt few shakes that were getting stronger and stronger.
Vitu vilianza kuanguka kutoka mezani. ||| Things started to fall down from the table.
Haikuwa wazi ni nini kilichotokea. ||| It was not clear what happened.
Hapakuwa na matangazo. ||| No announcements.
Kwanza tulidhani kuwa halikuwa jambo lenye uzito. ||| First, we were thinking that it wasn't serious.
Pengine kuna mtu aliyesimamisha treni kwa makosa. ||| Maybe someone stopped the train by accident.
Lakini makondakta wenye sura zenye hofu walianza kukimbia kila mahali wakikusanya magodoro, vitambaa vya mezani na maji. ||| But conductors with pale faces started running around collecting mattresses, tablecloths and water.
Walitutaka tusiondoke kwenye viti vyetu isipokuwa kama ni madaktari. ||| They asked us not to leave our seats unless we are doctors.

Uvumi ulianza kusambaa. ||| Some rumors started to go around.
Hatukuamini kuwa mabehewa mawili yalikuwa yametengana na yalikuwa mbali sana. ||| We didn't believe that two cars were disconnected and they were so far.
Baadaye tuligundua kuwa ilikuwa kweli. ||| Later, we fund out that it was true.
Tulitoka nje na tulitaka kusaidia. ||| We went out and wanted to help.
Tulikwenda mpaka behewa la tatu. ||| Went up untill the third car.
hatukutaka kuwa waduwazi ambao wanaongeza wingi wa watu bila fursa yoyote ya kusaidia. ||| We didn't want to be just gawkers and make a crowd without any opportunity to help.

Mara baada ya ajali, majukwaa ya uanahabari wa kijamii yalikuwa sehemu ya kwanza ambayo wanahabari wa Kirusi walikuwa wakitafuta habari. ||| Immediately after the crash, social media platforms became the first place where Russian journalist were looking for information.

Baadhi ya wanablogu walieza kughafirika kwao na ukweli kuwa ni watu wachache mno kutoka kwenye treni walitumia vyombo vya habari vya kijamii kutoa taarifa za kile kilichokuwa kinatokea., Na, inavyoonekana, kuna fafanuzi kadhaa zinazoelea ni kwa nini uanahabari wa kijamii haukuchukua nafasi kubwa katika upashaji wa habari za ajali ya Nevsky expressù. ||| Some bloggers expressed their frustration with the fact that so few people from the train used social media to report about what was happening. kuna watumiaji wa Twita 2,700 tu ambao wanaandika kwa lugha ya Kirusi. ||| there are only 2,700 Twitter users who write in Russian language.
Wakati huo huo, majukwaa maarufu ya kublogu nchini Urusi yangeweza kutumika ili kublogu moja kwa moja lakini, kama ilivyojadiliwa hapo juu, kuna mifano michache tu ya matumizi hayo. ||| At the same time, popular Russian blogging platformscould have been used for live reporting but, as discussed above, there is only a couple of examples of this use.
Ufafanuzi wa pili unahusiana na nafasi ya zana za mkononi na uunganishaji. ||| The second explanation is related to the role of mobile devices and connectivity.
Zana za mkononi zinaongezeka nchini. ||| The number of portable devices in the country is growing.
Warusi zaidi na zaidi wanaweza kutumia mtandao wa intaneti na zana nyingine za mtandaoni. ||| More and more Russians can use Internet and various Web-applications on the go.
Tabia hii ina nguvu katika maeneo ya Moscow na St. Petersburg. ||| This trend is especially strong in the area of Moscow and St. Petersburg.

Mawasilian ya simu yalikuwa mabaya sana. ||| The phone connection was very bad.
Inawezekana kuwa kila mtu alijaribu kupiga simu kwa wakati mmoja na mtandao ulielemewa. ||| Everyone probably tried to make a call at the same time and the net was overloaded.

Ndege ilianguka ndani ya mipaka ya mji ambako watu wengi waliweza kuona ni nini kilichokuwa kinatokea kutokea madirishani. ||| The plane crashed within the city borders where many people could see what happened right from their windows.
Ajali ya Nevsky expressù, kama ilivyoelezwa awali, ilitokea sehemu za vijijini. ||| The Nevsky expressù crash, as noted earlier, happened the rural area.
Habari zilizoandikwa kwa uanahabari wa kijamii kule Perm zilitokana na maelezo ya walioishuhudia ajali ambao hawakuwamo katika ajali (kwa bahati mbaya, hapakuwa na walionusurika kutoka katika ile ndege). ||| The social media coverage in Perm was based on the accounts of those who witnessed the crash but were not part of it (unfortunately, there were no survivors on the plane).
Mashahidi wote wa tukio la Nevsky Expressù walikuwa ni abiria katika treni. ||| All the witnesses of the Nevsky Expressù incident were passengers on the train.
Watu wengi walituma habari mpya juu ya ajali ya ndege kule Perm kwa kutumia tarakilishi za nyumbani. ||| Most people posted their updates on the plane crash in Perm using their home computers.
Walionusurika kwenye Nevsky Expressù walitegemea zana za mikononi. ||| The Nevsky Expressù survivors had to rely on their mobile devices.
Tofauti hizi zinabainisha kwa nini vyombo vya habari vya kiraia vilikuwa mbele katika ajali ya ndege na vilikaribia kutokuwepo kwenye tukio la Nevsky Express.ù ||| These differences explain why social media reporting was prevalent in the case of the plane crash and almost absent in the situation with Nevsky Express.ù

Video: Vijana duniani kote wajieleza kwa sekunde 60 ||| Video: Worldwide youth express themselves in 60 seconds
Mradi wa OneMinutesJr unawapa vijana wa umri wa kati ya miaka 12 na 20 kutoka kona mbalimbali za dunia fursa ya kujieleza, kusema na kujifunza ujuzi wa kutengeneza kazi za sauti-na-kuoangalia ili kuwasiliana zaidi ya mipaka yao, lugha zao na umbali zaidi kwa kutumia video ya sekunde 60. ||| The OneMinutesJr project gives young people between 12 and 20 years of age from many corners of the globe the opportunity to express themselves, speak out and learn audiovisual skills to communicate across borders, languages and distances through 60 second videos.
Mradi wa OneMinuteJr umetokana na jitihada za pamoja za Mfuko wa Utamaduni wa Ulaya, Mfuko wa One Minutes Jr na Unicef, vile vile na mashirika mwenza mengineyo. ||| The OneMinutesJr project results from the joint effort of the European Cultural Foundation, the One Minutes Jr. Foundation and Unicef, as well as other partner organizations.

Mwangwi wa Sakata la Maziwa China katika Afrika ||| Ripples of the China Milk Scandal in Africa
Nchini China inakadiriwa kuwa watoto 13,000 wameugua tangu sakata la maziwa yasiyofaa kuibuka. ||| In China, an estimated 13,000 children have fallen ill since the tainted milk scandal broke.
Ushawishi na nguvu za China vimeongezeka Afrika, kama ulivyoongezeka uagizwaji wa bidhaa za kila namna, kuanzia viatu vya mazoezi mpaka chakula aina ya tambi. ||| Chinese influence has grown in Africa, as have imports of all kinds products, from running shoes to instant noodles.

Kutoka Dakar, Bloga Naomed wa Le Blog Politique du Senegal ameandika mchezo huu mdogo wa kuigiza kuhusu dawa ijulikanayo kama melamine,ù jina la hiyo dawa ambayo iliongezwa kwenye maziwa ili kudanganya ubora wa maziwa hayo. ||| Blogging from Dakar, Naomed of Le Blog Politique du Senegal penned this short satire, a play on melamine,ù the name of the chemical which was added to the fake milk.
(Melamineù inakaribiana sana kimatamshi na neno melanine,ù ambalo kwa Kifaransa ni neno linalomaanisha melanin): ||| (Melamineù sounds very close to melanine,ù the French word for melanin):
Kushoto kwangu, mwanao mdogo mchangamfu, anayeonekana wa kawaida kabisa mwenye rangi ya chokleti aliyorithi kutoka kwa baba na mama yake. ||| To my left, your charming little child, the youngest, completely normal and of the chocolate color he inherited from his father and mother.
Kulia kwangu, kuna bilauri ya maziwa, inayoonekana kama ni ya dhati. ||| To my right, a glass of milk, seemingly honest.
Ni bilauri ya maziwa ya Kichina, kwa maneno mengine, imechanganyika mpaka chembe chembe ya mwisho ya casein. ||| A glass of Chinese milk, in other words, contaminated to the last molecule of casein.
Lazima tuwe wakweli, siyo maziwa yote ya Kichina yalichanganywa na vitu visivyofaa, lakini ni kama kamari; wale wanaoshinda zaidi ni wale wasiocheza kabisa. ||| Let's be honest, not all Chinese milks are contaminated, but it's a bit of a gamble; those who win the most are those who don't play at all.

Kama kawaida, unachelewa kazini kama kawaida yako. ||| As usual, you're late for work as usual.

Kulikoni? ||| What's going on?

Kadhalika katika namna ya utani, msomaji mwingine, Thomas anajibu: ||| Equally tongue-in-cheek, a reader, Thomas, responds:

Japan: Mkeo anapougua ||| Japan: When Your Wife is Sick
Pale utamaduni wa mifugo ya mashirikaù au kwa maneno mengine utamaduni wa ujumla wa wafanyakaziù na maadili ya ndoa vinapogongana zaidi ya watu 300 walitoa majibu kuhusiana na swali lililoulizwa kwenye jukwaa kubwa la mijadala lijulikanalo kama Hatsugen Komachi: Je, mwanaume aombe ruhusa kazini pale mkewe anapougua? ||| When Japanese corporate livestockù culture and values on marriage collide more than 300 people responded to this question on the mega forum Hatsugen Komachi: Should a husband take time off work when his wife is sick?
Rina amekuwa akiishi kwenye ndoa kwa miaka 8 sasa na binti yake anasoma darasa la tatu. ||| Rina has been married for 8 years and has a daughter in the third grade.
Anataka kutalikiana na anarejea tukio moja katika ndoa yake ambalo limebaki katika akili yake tangu wakati huo. ||| She is getting divorced and recounts an early episode in her marriage that has stuck in her mind since then.
Wakati binti yao alipokuwa akingali mchanga, Rina alinyong'onyea sana kwa sababu ya kukosa usingizi kutokana na kulia sana kwa binti yao nyakati za usiku. ||| When their daughter was a baby, Rina became very run down from sleep deprivation due to her night crying.

Sidhani kama ni jambo la kawaida kwa mume kutofika kazini kwa sababu mkewe anaumwa, labda kama inampasa kulazwa hospitalini. ||| I don't think it's normal for a husband to take a day off from work because his wife is sick, unless it requires a hospital stay.

naye anakumbuka jambo kama hilo. ||| recalls a similar experience.

Kwangu mimi huyu ni mume anayenijali kwa kufanya vitendo hivi. ||| To me, he's a caring husband for doing these things.

Nafikiri mumeo anataka kukaa nyumbani, lakini anashindwa. ||| I think your husband wants to stay home, but he can't.

Mexico: Uandishi Kutoka Gerezani ||| Mexico: Writing from Jail
Enrique Aranda Ochoa siyo mwandishi wako wa Ki-Mexico wa kawaida: Enrique alikamatwa mwaka 1997 na alituhumiwa kwa utekaji nyara, kiasi cha kumpelekea kuhukumiwa kwenda jela kwa miaka 50. ||| Enrique Aranda Ochoa is not your average Mexican writer: Enrique was arrested in 1997 and convicted of kidnapping with a sentence of 50 years in prison.

Katika eneo la mnara wa maji unaojulikana kama Njiwa wa Amani, Sicilia alieleza kwamba kupungua kwa idadi ya washiriki kulidhihirisha kwamba watu wamejifunza kuvumilia yasiyovumilika na kwamba kwa kuwa ni mwaka wa uchaguzi, basi jamii yenyewe ndiyo iliyokuwa katika hali ya kupata hasara zaidi. ||| At the fountain of the Peace Dove, Sicilia pointed out that the absence of more attendants was explained because people have learned to tolerate the intolerable and that the biggest loser, facing an election year, was the society itself.

Kongo: Utata Watawala Goma ||| Congo: Confusion Reigns in Goma
Miezi miwili iliyopita mapigano yamezuka tena katika jimbo la mashariki la Kivu katika Jamhuri ya Kidemokrasia ya Kongo kati ya kundi la upinzani linaloongozwa na Jenerali laurtent Nkunda na majeshi ya serikali, kinyume na makubaliano ya amani yaliyotiwa saini mwezi januari. ||| Two months ago fighting resumed in the DR Congo's Eastern province of North Kivu between the rebel group led by Laurent Nkunda and government forces, in violation of a peace accord signed in January.
Watu wapatao 250 000 wameteguliwa kutoka kwenye makazi yao tangu machafuko yalipolipuka tena mnamo mwezi wa Agosti, na kupelekea idadi ya watu waliopoteza makazi yao kufikia zaidi ya milioni 2 katika ukanda huo. ||| As many as 250,000 people have been displaced since the violent conflict re-ignited in August, bringing the region's total displacement figure to over 2 million.
Vikundi vya raia wenye hasira vimekuwa vikishambulia ofisi za Umoja wa Mataifa huko Goma, mji mkuu wa jimbo la Kivu ya Kaskazini, vikundi hivyo vimekasirikia Umoja wa Mataifa kwa kushindwa kuwalinda. ||| Mobs of angry civilians have been attacking UN offices in Goma, North Kivu's provincial capital, infuriated that the UN hasn't been able to protect them.
Fred R. akiandika katika Extra-Extra anaelezea mazingira ya nyuma ili kuweza kufahamu kwa nini umma umeghafirika: ||| Fred R. at Extra-Extra gives some background to understand the population's frustration:
 jukumu (la kuleta amani na usalama kwa kumaliza janga la majeshi ya kigeni na wanamgambo wa ndani) liliwaangukia majeshi yaliyojaa tahadhari, na yaliyoelemewa kikazi kupindukia ya Umoja wa mataifa pamoja na jeshi la Taifa lililojaa rushwa na uzembe ambalo liliundwa na mjeshi pinzani yaliyokuwa yakipigana huko nyuma. |||  the task (of bringing peace and security by ending the plague of foreign armed groups and local militias) fell to cautious, over-stretched UN forces and a corrupt, inept national army barely that was composed of former warring factions.
Ndani ya nchi hii kubwa iliyogawanyika katika vitongoji visivyo rahisi kuvifikia, haingekuwa jambo rahisi kutatua matatizo yote ya rushwa, uzembe, ushindani wa kikabila pamoja na ushindani wa kutaka ukubwa. ||| With the huge country split into myriad, inaccessible local enclaves, it was never going to be easy to resolve all the problems of corruption, mismanagement, inter-ethnic rivalries and power struggles.
Lakini kipindi kilichofuata baada ya uchaguzi mkuu kilitoa mwanya wa fursa kwa serikali mpya kuunganisha nchi kwa visheni au malengo makuu yaliyo wazi (kwa msaada wa Umoja wa Mataifa) vikiungwa mkono na mkondo wa sheria. ||| But the immediate post-election period offered a real window of opportunity for the new government to unite the country behind a clear vision and (with United Nations support) determined backing for the rule of law.
Walipoteza mwanya huo. ||| They blew it.

Maandamano nje ya boma la Umoja wa Mataifa yaligeuka kuwa ghasia mwanzoni mwa juma wakati wenyeji wa mji wa Goma waliporusha mawe kwenye boma hilo kutokana na kukata tamaa. ||| Protests outside the United Nations compound turned violent earlier this week as residents of Goma hurled rocks at the compound in frustration.
Kwa bahati mbaya, majeshi ya kulinda amani hayawezi kuzuia mashabulizi hayo bila ya kuongezewa vikosi. ||| Unfortunately, the peacekeeping mission cannot repel this attack without reinforcement.

Michelle F. kwenye blogu ya Stop The Genocide anakokotoa picha ya majeshi yenye silaha aliyoiita supu ya majeshi yenye silaha kwa herufiù katika Jamhuri ya Demokrasia ya Watu wa Kongo kwa wale ambao hawajui ni nani wahusika wakuu kwenye mzozo huu: ||| Michelle F. at the Stop Genocide blog offers a breakdown of the alphabet soup of armed elementsù in the People's Democratic Republic of Congo for those confused about the actors in this conflict:
Jenerali Laurent Nkunda na chama chake cha Taifa kwa Ajili ya Kulinda Watu au Congres National pour la Defense du Peuple anadai kupigana kwa ajili ya kuwalinda Wananchi wa Kongo wa kabila la Watusi dhidi ya wageni wasioalikwa na wala kutakiwa nchini humo, ||| General Laurent Nkunda and his Congres National pour la Defense du Peuple claim to fight for the protection of the Congolese Tutsi population from the Democratic Republic of Congo's most uninvited and unwelcome guests,
Jeshi la Wanademokrasia kwa Ajili ya Ukombozi wa Rwanda, Forces Democratiques de Liberation du Rwanda, au Interahamwe, waliondesha mauaji ya kimbari nchini Rwanda mwaka 1994, amabo wameweka kambi huko mashariki ta Jamhuri ya Kidemokrasia ya Kongo baada utawala wao wa vitisho nchini mwao. ||| The Forces Democratiques de Liberation du Rwanda, or Interahamwe, the perpetrators of the 1994 Rwandan genocide, who set up shop in the eastern DRC following their reign of terror in their own country.
Majeshi ya FDLR hivi sasa yanajumuisha makuruta wengi kutoka Kongo, pamoja na watoto. ||| The FDLR's ranks now include a substantial number of Congolese recruits, including chidlren.
Jeshi la Wananchi wa Kongo Forces Armes de la Republique Democratique du Congo (FARDC), ambao huko nyuma walijulikana kama mamahiri wa kila jambo ambalo jeshi la wananchi halitakiwi kufanya, na ||| The Forces Armes de la Republique Democratique du Congo (FARDC), the Armed Forces of the DRC, past masters of doing everything a national army is not supposed to do, and

Ofisi ya Kimataifa ya Wakimbizi, Refugees international inaeleza kuwa MONUC wamo kati-ya-jiwe-na-pahala-pagumu nchini humo. ||| Refugees International describes MONUC's rock-and-a-hard-place here.
Siku nne zilizopita waasi wa CNDP waliteka kambi kubwa ya jeshi huko Rumangabo kadhalika makao makuu ya Mbuga za Taifa za Virunga zenye ukubwa wa Maili Mraba 3000 (Kilometa za mraba 7,800) ambazo ni makazi ya sokwe wa milimani wapatao 200 kati ya jumla ya sokwe 700 wa aina hiyo duniani. ||| Four days ago the CNDP rebels seized a major military camp at Rumangabo as well as the headquarters of the 3,000 square mile (7,800 square kilometer) Virunga National Park that is home to 200 of the 700 endangered mountain gorillas in the world.
Waasi hao wamewahi kuitumia mbuga hiyo huko nyuma lakini walikuwa hawajawahi kuitumia kama makao yao makuu. ||| The rebels have used the park as a base but had never seized its headquarters before.
Mkurugenzi wa mbuga hiyo, Emmanuel de Merode, anaandika kuhusu matukio ya Jumapili katika blogu rasmi ya ya Mbuga za Virunga: ||| The director of the park, Emmanuel de Merode, wrote about the events on Sunday at the official Virunga Park blog:
Mapambano yamezingira kabisa kituo cha mbuga na walinzi wa doria mbugani wamelazimika kukimbilia misituni ili kuokoa maisha yao. ||| Fighting has now totally engulfed the park station and our Rangers have been forced to flee into the forests for their lives.
Waasi ndio wakazi pekee wa kituo cha mbuga cha Ramangabo hivi sasa. ||| The rebels now are the only occupants of the park station at Rumangabo.
Hili halijawahi kutokea wakati wowote kabla. ||| This has never happened before.
Huu ni wakati mgumu. ||| This is a serious time.
Tunahitajika kuwafikisha walinzi wetu wa doria mbugani wapatao 50 na zaidi mjinin Goma kwenye usalama, Kilometa zipatazo 45 kusini mwa Rumangabo. ||| We need to get our 50+ Rangers back to safety in Goma, 45km south of Rumangabo.
Barabara kuu imefungwa kutokana na mapambano hivyo wanatembea kwa miguu kukatiza misitu kusini mwa mbuga, kuelekea Kibumba, takriban kilometa 20 hivi zaidi,ambako tunatarajia kwenda kuwachukua kwa kutumia malori. ||| The main road is blocked because of the fighting so they are walking through the forests of the park south, to Kibumba, about 20km away, where we aim to pick them up in trucks.
Tunajaribu kuendelea kuwasiliana nao kwa simu lakini hawana nguvu za betri (mawe) ya kutosha kwenye simu zao. ||| We are trying to maintain phone contact but they don't have much battery life in their phones.
Siku mbili baadaye, 12 katika wale askari wa doria waliokuwa wakikimbia katika misitu waliokolewa na kupelekwa Goma. ||| Two days later, 12 of the 53 rangers that had to flee into the forest were rescued and brought to Goma.
Innocent Mburanumwe alielezea jinsi alivyokuwa mchovu, mwenye kiu na njaa wakati timu iliyotokea Goma ilipowakuta na kuwaokoa: ||| Innocent Mburanumwe described how tired, thirsty and hungry they were when the Goma team found them:
Askari doria wa mbuga walianza safari Jumapili mnamo saa 3 asubuhi wakiwa kundi la watu 14 kadhalika walikuwa na wanajeshi 4 ambao pia walikuwa wanwakimbia waasi. ||| The Rangers started off on Sunday at 9am as a group of 14 and also with 4 members of the military who were also fleeing the rebels.
Walikatiza mbugani, wakitarajia kutokeshezea barabarani, lakini walisikia milio ya mabomu na na mizinga na hivyo iliwabidi kurudi tena msituni. ||| They walked through the park, often trying to emerge onto the road, but heard many bombs and mortars and so had to go back into the forest.
Bila ya maji walianza kufyonza mawe ili kutuliza kiu, pia walijaribu kunyonya umande kutoka kwenye matope kwa kuweka kitambaa kati ya midomo yao na tope lenye nyevunyevu. ||| With no water they tried licking rocks to quench their thirst, and also tried sucking up the moisture from the mud, by putting a piece of clothing between their mouth and the moist mud.
Jumatano, msemaji wa CNDP alitangaza kusitishwa kwa mapigano, japokuwa hali huko Goma iliendelea kuwa kutoeleweka. ||| On Wednesday, a spokesperson of the CNDP announced a unilateral ceasefire, although the situation on the ground in Goma remains chaotic.
Kama ambavyo Kate Cronin-Furman kutoka blogu ya Wronging Rights anavyodokeza, kila mmoja inaonekana kuwa anajiandaa na vita, pengine kwa vile Nkunda huko nyuma amewahi kuonyesha kutoelewa maana ya neno usitishwaji wa mapigano.ù ||| As Kate Cronin-Furman from the blog Wronging Rights points out, everyone seems to be preparing for war anyway, probably on account of Nkunda's previously-demonstrated questionable grasp of the word cease-fire.ù

Goma ni vurugu tupu. ||| It's total chaos in Goma.
Nimeelezwa, kupitia simu mbalimbali na jumbe fupi za simu za viganjani, kwamba jeshi limeweka silaha chini huko Kibumba, malili 12 kaskazini ya Goma, na wanawakimbia waasi. ||| I am being told, through various phone calls and text messages, that the army have now laid down their weapons at Kibumba, 12 miles north of Goma, and are fleeing the rebels.

Waasi wa CNDP waasi wa Nkunda wanaushikilia Kiwanja na Rutshuru na wamesimika utawala wao kwenye eneo hilo. ||| The CNDP rebels Nkunda's rebels are in total control of Kiwanja and Rutshuru and have put in their own administration for the area.

Dawn Hurley, mfanyakazi wa kimataifa aishiye Goma anaandika katika blogu yake From Congo kuhusu ukosefu wa uhakika na hofu usiku unapoingia ||| Dawn Hurley, an American expatriate living in Goma, writes in her blog From Congo about the uncertainty and fear when night falls
Usiku hapa unaweza kuwa ni jambo la kutisha. ||| The night here can be a scary thing.
Mchana, maisha yanaonekana kuwezekana mjini Goma. ||| During the day, life seems tenable in Goma.
Lakini usiku huingia majira ya 12.30 hapa na kuanzia hapo mpaka asubuhi kila mmoja na lwake. ||| But night falls around 6:30 here and from then until morning everyone is on their own.
Watu wengi hawana magari, kwa hiyo hawawezi kwenda popote baada ya kuingia giza. ||| Most people don't have cars, so they can't go anywhere after dark.
Na siku hizi, haipendekezwi hata kuendesha gari wakati wa usiku. ||| And these days, even driving around in a car at night isn't recommended.
Watu wengi hawana umeme, kwa hiyo mara nyingi huketi na familia kwenye vibanda vyao, wakijiombea salama, wakisikiliza miwangwi ya risasi ikirindima mjini, huku wakisubiri nuru ya asubuhi. ||| Most people don't have power, so they are often sitting in small shacks with their families, praying for the best, listening to shots echo through town, and waiting for daylight.
Hakuna simu ya dharura ya 911 ya kupiga kama una tatizo. ||| There is no 911 to call if you have a problem.
Watu huwaita marafiki ambao wana kidogo cha kutoa, ghairi ya sauti iliyo upande wa pili wa simu. ||| At best people call their friends, who have little to offer, other than a voice on the other end of the line.

Tulipitisha usiku mzima tukiwa tumejifungia, huku milio ya risasi ikizingira kote. ||| We spent the night locked up, gunshots resounding everywhere.
Jeshi la Kongo lililaumiwa lakini nina hakika kwamba, kulikuwako pia wanajeshi wa Nkunda waliojipenyeza ili kuamsha hofu. ||| The Congolese army was blamed but there were also, I'm certain, soldiers infiltrated by Nkunda in order to raise the panic.
Wengine wao pia walikuwa wakitafuta pesa na waliua watu watatu. ||| Some of them were here also looking for money and they killed three people.
Waliwatisha MONUC na kuwatupia risasi. ||| They intimidate MONUC as well and they shoot their plances.
Mbali na hilo uwanja wa ndege haujachukulia na ndege zinaweza kutua. ||| In spite of this the airport hasn't been taken and the aircrafts can land.
Magereza yamefurika watu waliokamatwa na polisi na jeshi. ||| The prisons are bursting with people that have been detained by the police and the army.
Tunajaribu kutengeneza orodha ya wafungwa, na kuwapata wakiwa ndani ya mapango yao. ||| We are trying to make a list of the prisoners, to find them in the dungeons.
Wanajeshi wa serikali hawajakimbia wote, baadhi bado wanapigana huko Rutshuru ||| The government soldiers haven't all fled, some of them are still fighting around Rushuru

Hatimaye nimefahamu lile jambo ambalo nimelisoma kwenye vitabu, ambapo waandishi wakongwe huliongelea kuhusu hisia ya kukata tamaa inayowapata wanapotaka kurejea kwenye maeneo yaliyoharibiwa kabisa ambayo waliwahi kuyaandika wakati mambo yalipochukua mkondo mbaya zaidi. ||| I finally understand that thing I've read about in books, where hardened correspondents talk about the desperation they feel to return to the completely screwed places they've covered when things take a turn for the worse.
Inamaanisha jambo jingine wakati unafahamu fika sehemu hiyo ikoje, na kuna jambo linalotafuna ndani yako, likikuita kurejea tena huko. ||| It means something different when you know how that place looks in real life, and something gnaws at your gut, beckoning you back.

Mgomo huo uliofanyika baada ya Chama cha Walimu Tanzania, kupitia Rais wake Bw. ||| The strike came after the Teacher's union, through their president Mr.Gratian Mukoba, gave the government a 48-hours notice on 28 July, 2012.

Nadharia ya Pembe Tatu za Maisha inaeleza kimsingi kwamba sehemu nzuri ya kujikinga wakati wa tetemeko siyo chini ya samani, bali pembeni ya samani imara; kwa njia hiyo, ikiwa kipande cha samani kitavunjwa na vitu vinavyoporomoka, hakitamuangukia mtu aliyejikinga chini yake. ||| The Life Triangle theory basically states that the safest place to hide in an earthquake is not under furniture, but besides a strong piece of furniture: that way, if the piece of furniture is crushed by falling materials, it will not collapse on the person hiding under it.
Na badala yake, mtu huyo atakuwa salama katika nafasi iliyojitengeneza pembeni ya samani. ||| Instead, the person will be safe in the pocket created on the object's side.

Bolivia: Wanaharakati Washinikiza Upatikanaji Nafuu wa Mtandao wa Intaneti ||| Bolivia: Activists Push for Better Internet Connectivity
Wanablogu na wanaharakati wanatetea haki ya kupata kiwango cha chini kinachokubalika cha kasiù ya kuunganishwa na mtandao wa intaneti nchini Bolivia. ||| Bloggers and activists are advocating for universal access and minimum acceptable speedsù for Internet connections in Bolivia.
Kama ilivyokuwa imeripotiwa na Global Voices, Mkutano wa kwanza wa kitaifa wa Kukuza Uunganishwaji wa Intanenti nchini Bolivia National Meeting to Promote Connectivity in Bolivia ulifanyika mwishoni mwa Januari 2012. ||| As previously reported on Global Voices, the first National Meeting to Promote Connectivity in Bolivia took place in late January 2012.

Duran kutoka Palabras Libres, who met aliyekutana na Rais wa chembaù, Ms Gabriela Montao. ||| After the event, a group of activist continued to advocate, like blogger Mario R. Duran from Palabras Libres, who met with Bolivia's upper Chamber President, Ms. Gabriela Montao.
Kampeni hiyo ilitafuta pia kujulisha na kukuza uelewa wa masuala na vikwazo vinavyotokana na hali ya sasa ya mtandao. ||| The campaign is also seeking to inform and raise awareness on the issues and limitations of the current connectivity conditions.
Kikundi hicho kinakutana kuunga mkono tovuti ya Mtandao zaidi na nafuu kwa ajili ya Bolivia. ||| The group is gathering support at the site More and better Internet for Bolivia.
Tovuti inatafuta usawa katika upatikanaji wa mtandao wa intanenti kwa wa-Bolivia ||| The website seeks equality in Internet access for Bolivians
Usiote kupata mtandao wa kasi kubwa ila dai kasi ya kiwango cha kawaida kinachokubaliwaù. ||| Do not dream of super speeds but do demand the minimum acceptable speedù.
Wahitajika-Upatikanaji Nafuu wa Mtandao kwa wa-Bolivia wote. ||| Wanted Better Internet Access for all Bolivians.
Mchoro wenye taarifa umekuwa ukisambaa katika majukwaa ya vyombo vya habari vya kiraia kuonyesha kwamba Bolivia ni kati ya maeneo ya mwisho kabisa katika sekta ya ubora wa kasi ya mtandao barani Amerika ya Kusini. ||| An infographic that has been circulating on social media platforms shows that Bolivia is among the last places in connectivity and bandwidth in Latin America.
Mchoro huo unaonyesha pia kwamba nchini Bolivia, Megabaiti moja kwa sekunde inagharimu kati ya mara 6 na 11 zaidi ya inavyokuwa katika nchi nyingine za jirani kama Paraguay, nchi ambayo ina eneo dogo sana la ardhi. ||| It also shows that in Bolivia, one Mbps costs between 6 and 11 times more than in neighbouring countries including Paraguay, also a land-locked country.

Katika sehemu nyingi za nchi, giza linatawala na majenereta yamechukua nafasi kama vyanzo vya nishati ya umemeù Inasema blogu ya Adebayo. ||| In most parts of the country, darkness pervades and generators have taken over as the source of powerù, says Adebayo's blog.

Posti hii ni sehemu ya habari zetu maalumu za Maandamano ya Bahrain 2011. ||| This post is part of our special coverage of Bahrain Protests 2011.
Baada ya video ya kibaoù cha polisi wa Bahrain kusambaa sana mtandaoni Waziri wa Mambo ya Ndani alitoa tamko akiomba kuwayeyote aliyepiga picha tukio hilo aliripoti haraka ù kwa mamlaka zinazohusika. ||| After Bahrain's police Slapù video went viral the Minister of Interior issued a statement in which he asked that anyone who films such an event should report it immediatelyù to the authorities.
Siku mbili baadae, na kinyume na kauli hiyo, watu wengi walishangazwa na kukamatwa kwa mpiga picha. ||| Two days later, and in contrast with such statements, many were shocked at the news of the arrest of a photojournalist.
Ahmed Humaidan kutoka Kituo cha Biashara cha Jiji la Bahrain amekamatwa na bado hajulikani aliko tangu jana usiku. ||| Arrested and still missing youth photographer Ahmed Humaidan from Bahrain City Center Mall yesterday late night.
Zaidi ya polisi kanzu 15 walimkamata Humaidan kutoka katika Kituo cha biashara Jijini Bahrain ||| More than 15 undercover police arrested Humaidan from Bahrain city center

Ahmed Ismail ni mpiga picha za video ambaye aliuawa mjini Salambad mwaka jana wakati alipiga picha za maandamano. ||| Ahmed Ismail is a videographer who was killed in Salambad last year while filming a protest.
Alipigwa risasi kutoka kwenye gari la kiraia. ||| He was shot from a civilian car.

Humaidan ameshinda zaidi ya tuzo za kimataifa 140 katika tasnia ya uandishi wa habari picha, na anachukuliwa kuwa mpigapicha bora wa pili wa Nchi za Kiarabu kushinda katika mashindano ya upigaji picha. ||| Humaidan has won more than 140 international awards in photojournalism, and he is considered the second most Arab photographer to win awards in photography competitions.

Hong Kong: Raia wasema òHapana' kwa uchaguzi wa meya usio wa kidemokrasi ||| Hong Kong: Citizens Say No to Undemocratic City Mayor Election
Miongoni mwa wajumbe wa Kamati ya Kumchagua Mtendaji Mkuu wa Hong Kong wapatao 1,200, wajumbe 689 walimchagua Leung Chun-ying kuwa meya mpya mnamo tarehe 25 Machi kufuatia ushawishi mkubwa uliofanywa na Ofisi ya Ushawishi ya Serikali Kuu ya Watu ya Hong Kong. ||| Among the 1,200 Hong Kong Chief Executive Election Committee members, 689 elected Leung Chun-ying to be the next city mayor on March 25 under the influence and active lobbying of the Liasion Office of the Central People's Government in Hong Kong.
Matokeo yalipotangazwa, maelfu ya waandamanaji walipinga uchezewaji huo wa mchakato wa uchaguzi. Waliendesha maandamano hayo nje ya ukumbi wa muda wa uchaguzi. ||| When the election result was released, thousands of demonstrators protested against the Beijing manipulation of the election process outside the temporary election venue.
Kura ya maoni ya kiraia ya majaribio ||| The mock civil referendum
Kabla ya uchaguzi, kati ya Machi 23 hadi 24, zaidi ya raia 220,000 wa Hong Kong walishiriki kwenye kura ya maoniù ya majaribio iliyoandaliwa na Programu ya Maoni ya Umma ya Chuo Kikuu cha Hong Kong ili kuonyesha kutoridhishwa kwao na uchaguzi wa kikundi kidogo cha watu na kudai haki yao ya kumchagua meya wa jiji. ||| Before the election, between March 23-24, more than 220,000 Hong Kong citizens had participated in the mock civil referendumù organized by the Public Opinion Programme of the Hong Kong University to express their discontent towards the small circle election and to assert their right to vote for the city mayor.
Licha ya mfumo wa kupiga kura kushambuliwa na òwaiba taarifa za mtandaoni, maelfu ya wapiga kura wenye kustahili (wakazi wa jiji walio na umri wa zaidi ya miaka 18) walisisitiza kutaka kupanga mstari nje ya vituo vya kupigia kura kusubiri zamu zao: ||| Despite the online voting system being attacked by hackers, thousands of legitimate voters (local residents aged over 18) insisted to queue outside polling stations to cast their ballots:
Kituo cha kupigia kura katika Chuo Kikuu ya Poly mnamo tarehe 24 Machi. ||| Polling station at Poly University on March 24.
Mtumiaji wa Facebook Leung Chau Ming aliyekuwa kwenye mstari wa kusubiri zamu nje ya moja ya vituo vya kupigia kura mnamo tarehe 23 Machi; alieleza namna alivyoguswa na yale aliyoyaona kupitia ukurasa wa Facebook wa tukio la kura ya maoni: ||| Facebook user Leung Chau Ming was queued outside one of the polling stations on March 23; he described the touching scene on the Facebook page of the civic referendum event:
Nilikuwa kwenye foleni. ||| I was in the queue.
Tulizingatia utaratibu licha ya upepo mkali. ||| We kept in order despite the gale.
(Walikuwepo) wazee, watu wazima na vijana. ||| (There were) old people, adults and young guys.
Hata kuna mama mmoja alimlisha mwanae huku akiwa kwenye foleni. ||| A mother even fed his son while queuing.
Ninaelewa vema kuwa licha ya mapambano na mikutano yote ya hadhara mnamo tarehe 4 Juni (siku ya mkesha wa kuwasha mshumaa), 1 Julai, na (mwaka huu) Machi 23 (maandamano ya kupinga uingiliaji wa Beijing kwenye uchaguzi), n.k. Pengine hatutaona matunda ya demokrasi katika kipindi cha uhai wetu, lakini kwa kizazi kifuatacho, kizazi kitakachofuata baada ya kizazi kijacho,  idadi N ya vizazi vijavyo. ||| I fully understand that despite all the struggles and rallies on June 4 (annual candle night vigil), July 1, and (this year) March 23 (rally against Beijing intervention on the election), etc, we probably will not see the fruit of democracy in our lifetime, but for our next generation, our next next generation, generations from now.
Tuna wajibu. ||| We have responsibilities.
Ni wajibu wa kila mkazi wa Hong Kong hapa, na sasa! ||| It is also the obligation of every Hong Konger here and now!
Thomas Pang naye alikuwa kwenye msululu wa kusubiri zamu, naye alieleza kwa nini alikuwa tayari kushiriki kwenye uchaguzi huo wa majaribio: ||| Thomas Pang was in the same queue with Leung and he explained why he decided to queue up for the mock election:
Hatimaye jumla ya watu 222,990 walishiriki kwenye uchaguzi huo wa majaribio, ambapo asilimia 54.6 walipiga kura bila kuandika chochote kwenye karatasi za kura. ||| Eventually, 222,990 people voted in the mock election, in which 54.6 percent cast blank votes.
Leung Chun-ying alipata tu asilimia 17.8 ya kura zote, ambapo matokeo yalikuwa kinyume kabisa na uchaguzi wa kundi lile dogo la wateule, ambao uliendeshwa katika Kituo cha Mikutano na Maonyesho cha Hong Kong. ||| Leung Chun-ying only got 17.8 percent of the votes, a huge contrast with the result of small circle election, which was held in the Hong Kong Convention and Exhibition Center.
Maandamano nje ya ukumbi wa jiji tarehe 25 Machi ||| Protest outside the city hall on March 25
Mnamo tarehe 25 Machi, zaidi ya watu 2,000 waliandamana nje ya ukumbi wa muda wa uchaguzi. ||| On March 25, more than 2,000 people protested outside the temporary election venue.
Huku wakiwa wamekasirishwa sana na ushindi wa Leung, walipambana na kusukumana na ukuta wa polisi. ||| Outraged by Leung's victory, they pushed the police barricades.
Waandamanaji wakisukumana na ukuta hai wa polisi mnamo tarehe 25 Machi. ||| Protesters pushing the police barricades on March 25.
Waandamanaji wakiwa wameketi nje ya ukumbi wa uchaguzi. ||| Protesters sitting outside the election hall.
Joshua Wong, ambaye ni mwanaharakati kijana, alifanya tafakari kuhusu maandamano na kuonyesha wazi huzuni yakehasa kwa kukosa utayari kwa watu katika kuchukua hatua: ||| Joshua Wong, a young activist, reflected upon the demonstration and expressed his disappointment with people's unwillingness to take action:
Nakumbuka nilikuwa nimeketi kando ya barabara kwenye Kituo hicho, kisha kuna mtu alipaaza saudi akisema, Leung ameshinda!' Watu walisimama na kutoa mguno wa hasira. ||| I remembered when I was sitting on the road outside the center, someone suddenly shouted, Leung has won!' People stood up and howled.
Wengi walipigwa na bumbuwazi. ||| They felt surprised.
Nilitarajia kwamba angeshinda, lakini sikutegemea kuwa angefanya hivyo katika raundi ya kwanza tu tena kwa kura 689. ||| I was prepared for his victory, but did not expect he could win in the first round with 689 votes.
Nilivunjika moyo niliporejea nyumbani, siyo kwa sababu ya ushindi wa Leung, bali hisia za umimi na kujitenga: Sijali, yeyote atakayekuwa Kiongozi Mkuu, hili si suala langu, ili mradi tu (jamii) iko salama na kila kitu ni shwari', Msukumo utasababisha fujo za kisiasa na kuharibu jina la Hong Kong. ||| I was heartbroken when I was back home, not because of Leung's victory, but the feeling of cynicism and detachment: Whoever will be the Chief Executive is not my concern, as long as (the society is) safe and harmonious', impulse will lead to political chaos and destroy Hong Kong's image.

Vile vile (Adeyepo) ni mchungaji kiongozi wa kanisa liitwalo Faith Tabernacle (Kanisa la Imani) linalomiliki jengo kubwa lenye uwezo wa kubeba watu waliokaa wapatao 50,000 kwa mara moja, likidhaniwa kuwa kubwa kuliko makanisa yote duniani kwa mujibu wa kitabu cha Kumbukumbu cha Guinesss. India: Gazeti pekee duniani linaloandikwa kwa mkono ||| India: The Last Handwritten Newspaper in the World
Magazeti ya mwanzo yalikuwa yakiandikwa kwa mkono Inawezekana kwamba hivi sasa gazeti la The Musalman pengine ndiyo pekee lililobaki linaloandikwa kwa mkono ulimwenguni. ||| The earliest forms of newspaper were handwritten and now The Musalman probably is the last handwritten newspaper in the world.
Gazeti hili linalochapishwa kwa lugha ya Ki-Urdu lilianzishwa mwaka 1927 na Chenab Syed Asmadullah Sahi ambapo hivi sasa linachapishwa kila siku katika jiji la Chennai huko India tangu kuanzishwa kwake. ||| This Urdu language newspaper was established in 1927 by Chenab Syed Asmadullah Sahi and has been published daily in the Chennai city of India ever since.
Anayeliendesha hivi sasa ni mjukuu wa Syed Asmadullah anayeitwa Syed Arifullah. Anasaidiwa na wataalamu wa miandiko wapatao sita ili kuchapisha gazeti hili la kurasa nne kila siku. ||| It is presently run by Syed Asmadullah's grandson Syed Arifullah and six skilled calligraphers work on this four pages newspaper everyday.
Huku likichapisha idadi ya nakala zipatazo 23,000, gazeti hili huchapisha habari mbalimbali zikiwemo zile za siasa, utamaduni na michezo katika lugha ya Ki-Urdu. ||| With a circulation of approximately 23,000 the paper covers news in Urdu language across a wide spectrum including politics, culture and sports.
Kufuatia maendeleo ya kiteknolojia siku hizi, ambayo yanasababisha magazeti katika muundo unaobebeka kuanza kupotea, na watu kusoma zaidi magazeti kwenye mtandao wa internet, uwepo wa gazeti hili ni tunu ya pekee. ||| With the recent technological advances, where paper newspapers are going extinct because people read them online, this personable touch is rare to find.
Gazeti hili huuzwa kwa Paise 75 (kiasi cha kama senti 2 za dola, au Sh40). ||| The price of this paper is 75 Paise (approximately 2 US cents).
Hivi sasa mhariri wa gazeti hilo ni Wb. Syed Arifullah. ||| Presently it is edited by Mr. Syed Arifullah.
Alichukua nafasi hiyo baada ya baba yake kufariki dunia. ||| He took over the charge after his father died.
Baba yake aliliendesha kwa miaka 40. ||| His father ran this paper for 40 years.
Lilianzishwa na kupewa muundo na babu yake mwaka 1927. ||| It was founded by his grandfather in 1927.
Gazeti limeendeleza mwonekano wake wa asili na halikupokea mabadiliko ya mwandiko wa kompyuta ya Ki-Urdu. ||| This paper has maintained its original look and had not compromised with the Urdu computer font.
Maandalizi ya gazeti huchukua takribani saa tatu kila siku. ||| Preparation of its every page takes about three hours.
Baada ya habari kupokelewa katika lugha ya Kiingereza kutoka kwa waandishi ambao wako kwenye ajira ya muda, inatafsiriwa katika lugha za Ki-Urdu na Katibis wataalamu wa mwandiko, wanaoenzi mwandiko wa toka zama za kale wa Ki-Urdu, wanaindika habari yote kwa mkono. ||| After the news is received in English from its part time reporters, it is translated into Urdu and Katibs writers, dedicated to the ancient art of Urdu calligraphy, pen down the whole story on paper.
Baada ya hapo, nakala hasi ya gazeti zima lililoandikwa kwa mkono inapelekwa kiwandani tayari kuchapigwa chapa.. ||| After that negative copy of the entire hand-written paper is prepared and pressed on printing plates.
Kuandika maandishi ya Ki-Urdu lilikuwa suala gumu sana; na pia kutumia mashine kuandika kwenye lugha hiyo hakukuwa na mvuto machoni kwa kulinganisha na kuandika kwa mkono. ||| Afsar Shaheen comments in a post of Luthfispace elaborating why lithography is still being adopted: Urdu type setting was very difficult; also, typeset work looked ugly in comparison to handwritten work.
Kwa hiyo Ki-Urdu kiliendelea kutumia sanaa ya kuandika kwa mkono wakati lugha nyingine zilichukua muundo wa miandiko ya mashine. ||| Therefore, Urdu resorted to lithography while other languages adopted typeset.
Baada ya kuingia kwa kompyuta, mwandiko wa Ki-Urdu ulichukua sura mpya, bora zaidi. ||| With the advent of computer, Urdu writing got great boost.
Ilimruhusu mtaalamu wa mwandiko kuandika bila kupata shida sana ya kiundishi. ||| It allowed calligraphic writing without the problems of lithography.
Hata hivyo, kitabu au gazeti lililoandikwa kwa mkono na mwandishi na kupata upigaji chapa mzuri ni zuri na linavutia sana machoni; wala mwandiko wa Ki-Urdu wa kompyuta hauwezi kufua dafu. ||| Yet, a book or newspaper written by a good katib and properly lithographed is very pleasing and beautiful; computer written Urdu is no match.

Ikiwa TPS imepelekea ongezeko la asilimia 20 kwa wastani wa pesa zinazotumwa na kila mhamiaji, tunaweza kutarajia ongezeko la dola 360 za pesa zinazotumwa kwenda Haiti katika 2010. ||| If the TPS resulted in a 20 percent increase in the average remittance per migrant, we would expect an additional $360 million remittance flows to Haiti in 2010.
Na zaidi ya hilo, kama hadhi ya TPS itaongezwa muda wa zaidi ya miezi 18 ambayo imewekwa sasa kuna uwezekano mkubwa wa kuongezwa muda wa (TPS) tukiangalia historia ya kuongezwa muda wa TPS kwa ajili ya El Salvador, Honduras, Nicaragua, Somalia na Sudani ziada katika fedha zinazotumwa nchini Haiti itavuka dola bilioni katika miaka mitatu. ||| What is more, if the TPS were to be extended once beyond the currently stipulated 18 months the extension is almost certain to happen, judging by the history of extensions of the TPS for El Salvador, Honduras, Nicaragua, Somalia and Sudan additional fund flows to Haiti would exceed a billion dollar over three years.

India: Waume Kuwalipa Wake Zao kwa Kufanya Kazi za Nyumbani ||| India: Husbands to Pay Wives for Doing Household Chores?
Wizara ya Umoja wa maendeleo ya wanawake na Watoto nchini India inaufikiria mswada ambao kama utapitishwa na bunge utahalalisha ulazima wa waume kumega sehemu ya mishahara yao na kuwalipa wake wasio na ajira kama ujira kwa kazi za nyumbani wanazozifanya. ||| The Union Women and Child Development Ministry in India is considering a draft bill which, if passed by parliament, would make it legally compulsory for husbands to pay out a portion of their monthly income to their homemaker wives, for doing household chores.
Kwa mujibu wa pendekezo hilo la wizara, mswada huo unaandaliwa kiasi kwamba utaruhusu kupima kiwango cha kazi iliyofanywa na akina mama wa nyumbani kwa mtizamo wa makubaliano ya kiuchumi na kutambua mchango huu katika uchumi kwa kuwafidia akina mama hawa wa nyumbani kulingana na kazi wanazozifanya. ||| As per the Ministry's proposal, a model is being framed which will allow for valuation of the work done by homemakers in economic terms and then recognition of this contribution to the economy by compensating homemakers for their labour.
Kwa mujibu wa sheria hiyo, wafanyakazi wa ndani wanachukuliwa kama  wahandisi wa kazi za nyumbani . ||| The proposed law is expected to refer to homemakers as home engineers.
Waziri Krishna Tirath alisema kuwa, kiasi hiki ambacho kinakadiriwa kati ya asilimia 10-20% ya mshahara wa mwezi wa mume, haipaswi kuchukuliwa kama mshahara kwa ajili ya kazi za nyumbani, bali unapaswa kuchukuliwa kama jambo la kuonesha heshima au jambo linalofanana na hilo. ||| Minister Krishna Tirath has said that this amount, which could be anywhere between 10-20% of the husband's monthly salary, should not be looked upon as salary for housework; rather it could be referred to as an honorarium or something similar.
Wakati waziri akiliona jambo hili kama hatua kubwa iliyopigwa kuhusiana na na wanawake kuwezeshwa, mswada huu wa sheria unajadiliwa vikali, nje ya mtandao wa intaneti na hata kwenye mitandao ya intaneti. ||| While the Minister sees this as a step forward in women's empowerment, the proposal is being debated hotly, both offline as well as online.

Chile: Mchakato wa Ujenzi Mpya Baada ya Tetemeko la Ardhi ||| Chile: The Process of Earthquake Reconstruction
Akihimiza Umoja wa kitaifaù katika viwanja vya wazi vya Concepcion mnamo tarehe 27 Machi, mwezi mmoja kamili baada ya nchi kupigwa na tetemeko baya kabisa, Rais Sebastian Piatera alitangaza Mpango uliobatizwa jina la Hebu Turejee kwenye Kaziù, ambalo ni vuguvugu lililoanzishwa na Serikali ya Chile ili kujenga mpya miundombinu ya nchi pamoja na majengo. ||| Calling for national unityù in Concepcion's main square on March 27, exactly a month after the devastating earthquake that hit Chile, President Sebastian Piatera announced Plan Let's Get to Work, an initiative of the Chilean government to reconstruct the country's infrastructure and housing.
Siku mbili baadaye, tarehe 29 Machi, Piatera pia alitangaza mpango wa kutoa ruzuku ya dola za Marekani 2,543 ili kuzisaidia familia zipatazo 195,950. ||| Two days later, on March 29, Piatera also announced a plan to provide a subsidy of United States Dollars 2,543 each to assist 195,950 families.
Huko Concepcion, Rais alieleza kwamba hatua za muhimu zilikuwa zimekwishaanza kuchukuliwa ili kujenga upaya madaraja, barabara, bandari na viwanja vya ndege. ||| In Concepcion, he explained that the necessary measures to reconstruct bridges, roads, ports, and airports were already underway.
Pia alitangaza kwamba vituo vya dharura vya afya vitasaidia kazi za mfumo mzima wa afya kuanzia mwezi Aprili, na kwamba feri na madaraja ya dharura kuvuka Mto Bio-Bio utasaidia katika usafirishaji wa mizigo mizito na vifaa kwenda San Pedro de la Paz na Talcahuano. ||| He also announced that emergency health posts will correct the deficiencies of the health care system starting in April, and that emergency ferries and bridges in the Bio-Bio River will allow for the transport of heavy loads of materials and supplies to San Pedro de la Paz and Talcahuano.
Hatimaye, Rais alieleza kwamba kutakuwa na mfuko maalumu ambao utagawanya jumla ya peso bilioni 8 (sawa na dola za Marekani milioni 15,107,160) kwa kupitia vocha maalumu zitakazogawanywa kwa familia zipatazo 200,000 ili ziweze kununua vifaa vya ujenzi. ||| Finally, the President highlighted a special fund that will distribute 8 billion pesos (15,107,160 United States Dollars) through vouchers given to more than 200,000 families to provide them with construction materials.
Julio Segovia, ambaye ni msomaji wa makala iliyochapishwa na gazeti la La Nacian na ambayo ndiyo ilibeba tangazo hilo la mfuko huo maalumu, alikosoa mfuko huo maalumu wa nyuma akisema: ||| Julio Segovia, a reader of the La Nacian newspaper article that informed about this announcement, criticized the special fund for housing:
Je, peso bilioni 8 ndiyo zitakazogawanywa kwa zaidi ya familia 200,000? ||| 8 billion pesos will be distributed between more than 200,000 families?
Na kwa kiasi hicho cha fedha familia hizo zinapaswa kujenga upya makazi yao? ||| With that amount they are meant to reconstruct their houses?
Yaelekea Piatera Rais ameanza kushindwa kaziù. ||| It seems that Piatera is falling shortù as President.
Mtumiaji wa Twita Viviana Meneses alipokea tangazo la Rais na kukubaliana na kauli iliyotolewa na Seneta Camilo Escalona wa kutoka Chama cha Kisoshalisti ambaye alipata kusema hapo kabla kwamba Rais hakuwa na mpango wowote wa maana wenye kuikwamua nchi kutoka katika tatizo hilo: ||| Twitter user Viviana Meneses reacted to the President's announcement and agreed with statements made by Senator Camilo Escalona of the Socialist Party, who had said earlier that the President did not actually have a structured plan:
